[2025-12-08T10:52:57Z] Akshay: The likely origin of this now ubiquitous software and API X is in the early 2000s at Stanford, where the first ever instance was called Brooke. CS PhD student Ian Buck had built his own video gaming setups with Nvidia GeForce cards, trying to jack up the performance of games like Doom and Quake, but with time he transitioned to exploring using ___ for general purpose computing tasks. Nvidia hired Buck who alongwith John Nickolls began the development process that eventually turned Brooke into X. In this they were supported by US govt agencies like DARPA. Today X underpins much of modern AI, ML and almost all large scale scientific computing.

[2025-12-09T14:36:52Z] Ryan Colaço: Hahah… thsi one was tricky to frame without giving it away too easily… ↵  Y is something we see and encounter and do everyday, Y is definitely existed for millennia. ↵ The feature X, however, is surprisingly a very young modification/innovation. It was only in the 7th century, in the monasteries of Ireland and Britain, that monks began introducing a certain innovation (X) so routinely and consistently that it eventually reshaped how Y is consumed all over the world. Earlier Greek and Roman texts had used it only sparingly, since fluent scholars didn’t really need the help. But for Irish monks wrestling with a foreign language, this tiny adjustment made everything clearer, copying safer, and even silent study faster. Today we take it so utterly for granted that it feels inseparable from the broader human system it belongs to. What is X, and what is Y, the larger system it transformed?

[2025-12-09T14:40:55Z] Ryan Colaço: X = Consistent word spacing ↵ Y = Writing / script ↵ Writing long predates medieval Europe, but routine, consistent word spacing is relatively late. ↵ Insular manuscripts (Ireland & Britain, 7th–9th c.) are where systematic spacing first appears. ↵ Classical Greek & Latin used _scriptio continua_, with spacing only used sporadically for novices. ↵ Scholars fluent in the language didn’t need spacing; Irish monks learning Latin did, so they innovated. ↵ Spacing later proved to speed silent reading and reduce copying errors, spreading across Europe.

[2025-12-09T15:43:23Z] Kumar Varun: “Lagawelu jab lipstick” ↵ Lagawelu ( “ when you apply” as in ‘lagati ho’ in Hindi )- Sanskrit root - lag/ lagn meaning ‘adhere / attach ‘  and then you add bhojpuri grammar and get bhojpuri verb ‘lagawelu’ ↵ jab ( when )- Persian origin meaning “when “ … absorbed in Urdu / Hindi / Awadhi and of course bhojpuri .. still meaning “ when “ ↵ Lipistic: from English lipstick ! ↵ So “ Lagawelu jab lipistic “ … “ when you apply lipstick “ ↵ So this one simple line combines so many languages in some sense ! Beauty of languages I guess .. ↵ Also what a rare group when can nerd about these things !

[2025-12-09T18:18:16Z] Akshay: In the initial days of X, many Indians were enthusiastic supporters. Even the famously pacifist gandhi actively exhorted Indians to sign up for X, naively hoping that his loyalty would be rewarded with democratic concessions after. Almost everyone expected X to be a short lived affair, ending in 1-2 years at most. However, as X wore on, the British became even more repressive, particularly for a certain reason Y. This was most pronounced in Punjab, where they bribed the lambardars and zamindars into aggressively doing Y, giving immense cash, titles such as ‘rai bahadur’ and some of the most coveted land parcels near the Indus river system canals in return. The administration particularly singled out ‘subversive’ men and suspected revolutionaries for Y, while the feudal lords targeted mostly  the poor, marginalized and powerless. Give X, Y.
